الفنون « الحد عند الأصوليين مرادف للمعرف وهو ما يميز الشيء عن غيره وذلك الشيء يسمى محدوداً ومعرفاً » ثم يفرق بين هذا الحد والحد الارسططاليسي . فالأول « يفيد تمييز صورة عما عداها » والثاني « يحصل في الذهن صورة غير حاصلة » ثم يتكلم عن أنواع الحد عند المناطقة ـ وينتهي إلى القول بأن هناك فارقاً بين الإثنين(١) ويرى الزركشي أن أئمة الكلام والأصول يرون أن القصد من الحد التمييز بين المحدود وغيره . ثم ينقل عن إمام الحرمين « أن القصد من التحديد في اصطلاح المتكلمين الفرق بخاصة الشيء وحقيقته التي يقع بها الفصل بينه وبين غيره . أما المناطقة فقالوا « إن فائدة الحد التصوير » (٢) أي تصوير الماهية . هناك إذن اختلاف كبير في تعريف الحد وغايته عند الأصوليين والأرسططاليسيين . فإن المنطق الأرسططاليسي يعتبر الإقتصار على تمييز المحدود عن غيره دون تتميم حقيقته بمقوماتها إخلالاً بالحد . فاذا عرفنا الإنسان بأنه جسم ناطق وحذفنا ـ ذو نفس حساس متحرك بالإرادة ـ اعتماداً على أنه لا شيء غيره جسم ناطق ، كان هذا التعريف غير تام . ولذلك لم يقبل إمام الحرمين الحد الأصولي ـ وهو من بين المتقدمين الوحيد الذي خالف هذا الاتجاه وأخرج حدوده على طريقة المنطق الأرسططاليسي ـ وإذا كان الحد عند المناطقة الأرسططاليسيين يفيد تصور المنطوق بعد أن لم يكن ، فالحد الحقيقي هو ما اشتمل على مقومات الشيء المشتركة والخاصة . فهو يتوقف ـ كما هو مفهوم ـ على معرفة جميع الذاتيات وترتيبها على الوجه الصحيح . ومعنى ترتيبها على الوجه الصحيح إيراد الجنس أولاً ، ثم الفصل ثانياً . أما الأصوليون فالبعض منهم أنكروا أن يتكون الحد من أي نوع من أنواع الماهيات(٣) وهؤلاء يكاد يكون الحد عندهم لفظياً بحتاً ، فيميز المحدود عن غيره بدون تقيد بفكرة الذاتيات أو العرضيات . والبعض الآخر يرى أن الحد يتكون من ماهية اعتبارية فيحدث الفرق بين المحدود وغيره بخاصة الشيء وحقيقته التي يقع بها الفصل بينه وبين غيره(١). وكلا الإتجاهين لا يوافق على استناد الحد الى فكرة الجنس والفصل الذاتيين كما يفهمها المناطقة الأرسططاليسيون . ولكن الفريق الثاني من الأصوليين اشترط مع ذلك الإطراد والإنعكاس أي يلزم من ثبوت الوصف ثبوت المحدود ومن إنتفائه انتفاؤه . يقرر إمام الحرمين أن « الإطراد والإنعكاس لا يتم الحد عند الأصوليين إلا بهما »(٢) . وإذا كان الحد عند الأرسططاليسيين هو تعريف الشيء بالتوصل إلى ماهيته . أي لا بد من معرفة الماهيات المختلفة تفصيلاً ، حتى يعلم المشترك بين الأشياء المشتركة في شيء واحد أي « الجنس » والقدر الذي ينفصل به كل واحدة منها عن الأخرى أي « الفصل » فمن الصعوبة التوصل اليه وقد لاحظ ابن سينا هذا من قبل . أما الحد الأصولي . فهو في غاية السهولة ، لأنه إذا كان الحد تفصيل ما دل عليه اللفظ إجمالاً ، فلا عسر في اقتناصه(٣) . يقول أبو البركات البغدادي رداً على ابن سينا « الحدود في غاية السهولة ، لأن الحدود هي حدود الأسماء ـ والأسماء أسماء الأمور المعقولة ـ وكل أمر معقول فلا بد وأن يعقل ـ أن كمال المشترك أي شيء هو وما هو ، وكمال جزء المميز أي شيء هو ـ فكان الحد سهلاً من هذا الوجه(٤) . ويقول فخر الدين الرازي في الملخص « الإنصاف إنه إن كان الغرض المقصود منه تفصيل مدلول الإسم كان سهلاً ، وإن كان الغرض معرفة الماهيات الموجودة كان ذلك في غاية الصعوبة »(٥) ويردد ابن تيمية أيضاً هذا « عسر الحد مبني على أنه تفصيل الماهية . أما إذا كان تفصيل الاسم فهو سهل »
The arts: 'The definition according to the usuliyyun is synonymous with identifier, and it is what distinguishes a thing from others, and that thing is called the defined and identified.' Then he distinguishes between this definition and the Aristotelian definition. The first 'benefits the distinction of a form from what is other than it,' and the second 'produces in the mind a form not previously present.' Then he speaks about the types of definition according to the logicians, and ends by saying that there is a difference between the two. Al-Zarkashi sees that the imams of kalam and usul hold that the purpose of definition is to distinguish the defined from others. Then he quotes Imam al-Haramayn: 'The purpose of definition in the terminology of the theologians is the distinction by the specific property of the thing and its reality by which the separation between it and other occurs. As for the logicians, they said, 'The benefit of definition is conceptualization,' i.e., conceptualization of the essence.' There is then a great difference in the definition and its goal according to the usuliyyun and the Aristotelians. For Aristotelian logic considers restricting to distinguishing the defined from others without completing its reality with its constitutive elements as a deficiency in the definition. If we define man as a rational body and omit 'having a sensitive soul moving by will' based on the fact that nothing else is a rational body, this definition would be incomplete. Therefore, Imam al-Haramayn did not accept the usuli definition – and he is among the early scholars the only one who opposed this trend and produced his definitions according to the Aristotelian method – and if the definition according to the Aristotelian logicians benefits the conceptualization of the term after it was not, then the true definition is what includes the common and specific constituents of the thing. It depends – as is understood – on knowledge of all the essential characteristics and their arrangement in the correct manner. And the meaning of their arrangement in the correct manner is presenting the genus first, then the differentia second. As for the usuliyyun, some of them denied that the definition is composed of any type of essences, and these, the definition according to them is almost purely verbal, distinguishing the defined from others without being tied to the idea of essential or accidental attributes. And others see that the definition is composed of an mental essence, thus effecting the difference between the defined and others by the specific property of the thing and its reality by which the separation between it and other occurs. Both trends do not agree on the definition being based on the idea of essential genus and differentia as understood by the Aristotelian logicians. However, the second group of usuliyyun stipulated along with that co-extensiveness and co-exclusiveness, i.e., it is necessary from the affirmation of the description the affirmation of the defined, and from its negation its negation. Imam al-Haramayn established that 'co-extensiveness and co-exclusiveness: the definition according to the usuliyyun is not complete except with both.' And if the definition according to the Aristotelians is defining a thing by reaching its essence, i.e., one must know the different essences in detail, so that one knows the common between things that share in one thing, i.e., 'the genus,' and the extent by which each one separates from the other, i.e., 'the differentia,' then attaining it is difficult, and Ibn Sina had noted this before. As for the usuli definition, it is extremely easy, because if the definition is a detailing of what the word indicates in summary, then there is no difficulty in its capture. Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi says in response to Ibn Sina: 'Definitions are extremely easy, because definitions are definitions of names – and names are names of intelligible matters – and every intelligible matter must be intellected – what is the common perfection, what it is and what it is, and what is the specific part perfection, what it is – thus the definition was easy from this aspect.' And Fakhr al-Din al-Razi says in al-Mulakhkhas: 'Fairness is that if the intended purpose of it is detailing the meaning of the name, it is easy; and if the purpose is knowledge of the existing essences, that is extremely difficult.' And Ibn Taymiyya also repeats this: 'The difficulty of definition is based on it being a detailing of the essence. As for if it is a detailing of the name, it is easy.'
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage critically examines the concept of 'hadd' (definition) as understood by two distinct schools: the Islamic legal theorists (usuliyyun) and the Aristotelian logicians. It opens by stating that for the usuliyyun, 'hadd' is synonymous with 'mu'arraf' (identifier), which is simply that which distinguishes a thing from other things. The defined object is called 'mahdud' or 'mu'arraf'. Then the author distinguishes this from the Aristotelian definition: the usuli definition yields a distinction of a form from what is other than it, whereas the Aristotelian definition produces a form in the mind that was not there before, i.e., it conveys the essence. The author notes that al-Zarkashi reports that the early theologians (mutakallimun) and usuli scholars believe the purpose of definition is merely distinction. He then quotes Imam al-Haramayn (Juwayni) who says that according to the theologians, definition aims to differentiate by the specific property and reality of the thing that separates it from others. By contrast, the logicians say the benefit of definition is 'taswir' (conceptualization), meaning the conceptualization of the essence (mahiyya). Thus, there is a major difference between the two groups regarding the definition and its goal. The Aristotelian logic considers restricting to mere distinction without completing the reality with its constitutive elements (muqawwimat) as a deficiency. The author gives an example: defining 'insan' (man) as 'rational body' (jism natiq) and omitting 'possessing a sensitive soul moving by will' (dhu nafs hassas mutaharrik bi al-irada) – assuming there is nothing else that is a rational body – would be incomplete. For this reason, Imam al-Haramayn rejected the usuli definition; he is noted as the only early scholar who opposed the usuli trend and formulated definitions according to the Aristotelian method. For the Aristotelians, the true definition includes both the common and specific constituents of the thing. This requires knowledge of all essential attributes (dhatiyyat) and their proper ordering: first the genus (jins), then the differentia (fasl). Next, the author describes the usuli positions. Some usuliyyun deny that definition is composed of any essence (mahiyya) at all; for them, definition is purely verbal, simply distinguishing without reference to essential or accidental attributes. Others hold that definition is composed of a mental essence (mahiyya i'tibariyya), creating the distinction by the specific property and reality that separate the defined from others. Both groups reject grounding definition on the idea of essential genus and differentia as understood by Aristotelians. However, the second group stipulates that the definition must be 'mutṭarid' (co-extensive) and 'mun'akis' (co-exclusive): the description must entail the defined and its negation must entail the negation of the defined. Imam al-Haramayn states that these two conditions are necessary for a complete usuli definition. The author then contrasts the difficulty of Aristotelian definition with the ease of usuli definition. Aristotelian definition aims to reach the essence, requiring detailed knowledge of different essences to identify the common genus and the differentia that separate each species. Ibn Sina had already noted the difficulty. The usuli definition, being a detailing of what the word indicates in summary, is easy to capture. The author supports this with quotes: Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi responds to Ibn Sina, arguing that definitions are easy because they are definitions of names, and names are names of intelligible matters; every intelligible matter can be understood, so its definition is easy. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi says that if the purpose is detailing the meaning of the name, it is easy; but if it is to know existing essences, it is extremely difficult. Ibn Taymiyya echoes this: difficulty arises only if the definition details the essence; if it merely details the name, it is easy.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Haramayn as quoted in the passage, what two conditions must a valid usuli definition satisfy?
A) It must include genus and differentia.
B) It must be co-extensive (ittirād) and co-exclusive (inkisās).
C) It must be purely verbal and avoid essence.

Key Takeaway
The usuliyyun define hadd as a tool for distinction, not necessarily for capturing essence, and they require it to be co-extensive and co-exclusive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the usuli definition of 'wudu' as 'washing specific limbs with water with intention.' Check whether this definition satisfies co-extensiveness and co-exclusiveness: does it apply to all valid wudu? Does it exclude non-wudu actions like bathing? Explain your reasoning.
?
Construct an Aristotelian definition of 'salah' using genus and differentia: what genus does salah belong to (e.g., 'physical worship') and what differentia distinguishes it from other acts of worship (e.g., 'specific postures and recitations')? Then compare this with a typical usuli definition.

The Two Conceptions of Definition: Aristotelian vs Usuli
Author contrasts Aristotelian and usuli definitions on ease and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Aristotelian and usuli definitions of hadd and identify their respective aims.

Core Idea
Definition in usul al-fiqh is about distinguishing meanings, not unveiling essences.

This passage presents a fundamental disagreement over the purpose of definition. The Aristotelian tradition, represented by Ibn Sina, sees definition as the key to understanding quiddity. The usuli tradition, exemplified by Imam al-Haramayn and others, views definition as a practical tool to clarify the meaning of a name. Understanding this difference is crucial for reading Islamic legal and theological texts correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate the description of the Aristotelian definition (based on genus and differentia aimed at quiddity) and the usuli definition (based on distinguishing properties or clarifying names).
2
Extract the aim of each definition
For Aristotelians, definition aims at knowing mahiyya (quiddity). For usuliyyun, definition aims at clarifying what the name indicates.
3
Note the difficulty assessment
The Aristotelians (Ibn Sina) find definition difficult because it requires detailed knowledge of quiddities. The usuliyyun (Abu al-Barakat, al-Razi, Ibn Taymiyya) argue it is easy because it only requires understanding names.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a definition from an Islamic discipline (fiqh, kalam), determine whether it follows the Aristotelian or usuli conception.
Remember that many Islamic texts blend both.

يرى أن الحد يتكون من ماهية اعتبارية فيحدث الفرق بين المحدود وغيره بخاصة الشيء وحقيقته التي يقع بها الفصل بينه وبين غيره. وكلا الاتجاهين لا يوافق على استناد الحد إلى فكرة الجنس والفصل الذاتيين كما يفهمها المناطقة الأرسططاليسيون. ولكن الفريق الثاني من الأصوليين اشترط مع ذلك الإطراد والإنعكاس أي يلزم من ثبوت الوصف ثبوت المحدود ومن انتفائه انتفاؤه. يقرر إمام الحرمين أن « الإطراد والإنعكاس لا يتم الحد عند الأصوليين إلا بهما ». وإذا كان الحد عند الأرسططاليسيين هو تعريف الشيء بالتوصل إلى ماهيته. أي لا بد من معرفة الماهيات المختلفة تفصيلاً، حتى يعلم المشترك بين الأشياء المشتركة في شيء واحد أي « الجنس » والقدر الذي ينفصل به كل واحدة منها عن الأخرى أي « الفصل » فمن الصعوبة التوصل إليه وقد لاحظ ابن سينا هذا من قبل. أما الحد الأصولي فهو في غاية السهولة، لأنه إذا كان الحد تفصيل ما دل عليه اللفظ إجمالاً، فلا عسر في اقتناصه. يقول أبو البركات البغدادي رداً على ابن سينا « الحدود في غاية السهولة، لأن الحدود هي حدود الأسماء ـ والأسماء أسماء الأمور المعقولة ـ وكل أمر معقول فلا بد وأن يعقل ـ أن كمال المشترك أي شيء هو وما هو، وكمال جزء المميز أي شيء هو ـ فكان الحد سهلاً من هذا الوجه. ويقول فخر الدين الرازي في الملخص « الإنصاف إنه إن كان الغرض المقصود منه تفصيل مدلول الإسم كان سهلاً، وإن كان الغرض معرفة الماهيات الموجودة كان ذلك في غاية الصعوبة » ويردد ابن تيمية أيضاً هذا « عسر الحد مبني على اعتقادهم أن المراد بالحد تصوره وليس كذلك ». فصعوبة التوصل إلى الحد إذن ناتجة من تعريف الحد الأرسططاليسي من أنه المعرف للماهية. أما إذا كان قصد به التمييز غير الذاتي بين المحدود وغيره، كان في غاية السهولة.
He holds that the definition (hadd) consists of an accidental quiddity, so it differentiates the defined from other things by a particular property of the thing and its reality by which distinction occurs. Both trends do not agree that the definition is based on the idea of essential genus and differentia as understood by the Aristotelian logicians. But the second group of legal theorists stipulated, along with that, consistency (ittiraad) and reversal (in'ikaas), i.e., from the established description the established defined follows, and from its negation its negation follows. Imam al-Haramayn stated: 'Consistency and reversal: the definition is not complete for the legal theorists except by them both.' And if the definition among the Aristotelians is the definition of a thing by arriving at its quiddity—that is, one must know the different quiddities in detail, so that the commonality among things sharing one thing, i.e., genus, and the amount by which each one is separated from the other, i.e., differentia, are known—then it is difficult to attain it, and Ibn Sina noted this before. As for the usuli definition, it is extremely easy, because if the definition is a detailed clarification of what the word indicates in summary, then there is no difficulty in capturing it. Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi said in response to Ibn Sina: 'Definitions are extremely easy, because definitions are definitions of names—and names are names of intelligible matters—and every intelligible matter must be intelligible—that the completeness of the common thing is what it is and what it is, and the completeness of the distinguishing part is what it is—so the definition was easy from this aspect.' Fakhr al-Din al-Razi said in al-Mulakhkhas: 'Fairness: if the intended purpose of it is to detail the meaning of the name, it is easy; but if the purpose is knowledge of existing quiddities, that is extremely difficult.' Ibn Taymiyya also echoes this: 'The difficulty of definition is based on their belief that by definition what is meant is conceptualization (tasawwur), but that is not the case.' Thus the difficulty of arriving at the definition results from the Aristotelian definition being that which defines quiddity. But if the intention is the non-essential distinction between the defined and other things, it is extremely easy.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of definition (hadd) from two contrasting perspectives: the Aristotelian logicians and the Islamic legal theorists (usuliyyun). The author first presents two trends among the usuliyyun regarding the nature of definition. The first trend holds that definition consists of an accidental quiddity that distinguishes the defined from other things by a particular property. The second trend, while not accepting the Aristotelian essential genus and differentia, adds the conditions of ittiraad (consistency) and in'ikaas (reversal): the definition must be such that whenever the defining description exists, the defined exists, and whenever it is absent, the defined is absent. Imam al-Haramayn affirms that no definition is complete among the usuliyyun without these two conditions. Then the author explains why the Aristotelian definition is difficult. For them, definition aims to reveal the quiddity (mahiyya) of a thing, requiring detailed knowledge of the common genus and the differentiating differentia. Ibn Sina himself acknowledged this difficulty. In contrast, the usuli definition is easy because it merely clarifies in detail what the name indicates in summary. Several scholars are quoted to support this view: Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi argues that definitions are simply definitions of names of intelligible matters, and every intelligible matter can be understood, so definition is easy. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi distinguishes between two possible aims of definition: if it is to detail the meaning of a name, it is easy; if it is to know essences, it is extremely difficult. Ibn Taymiyya asserts that the supposed difficulty is based on the mistaken belief that definition aims at conceptualization (tasawwur) of essences, whereas the actual purpose is not that. The passage concludes that the difficulty arises only from the Aristotelian view of definition as revealing quiddity; if definition is intended merely for non-essential distinction, it is extremely easy. All examples in the commentary are from the Islamic intellectual tradition.

الماهية

B) Aristotelian definition aims at quiddity; usuli definition aims at clarifying the name.
C) Aristotelian definition is easy; usuli definition is difficult.

Key Takeaway
The usuli conception of definition prioritizes practical clarity over metaphysical essence, making definitions easier to achieve.

Conditions of a Valid Definition in Usul al-Fiqh: Ittiraad and In'ikaas
Author contrasts Aristotelian and usuli definitions on ease and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of ittiraad (consistency) and in'ikaas (reversal) to evaluate a legal definition.

Core Idea
A valid usuli definition must satisfy consistency and reversal.

Imam al-Haramayn declared that no definition among the legal theorists is complete without the two conditions: ittiraad and in'ikaas. This lesson unpacks these conditions and shows how they function as practical tests for legal definitions.

Guided Path
1
Define ittiraad and in'ikaas
Ittiraad: whenever the defining description is present, the defined must be present. In'ikaas: whenever the defining description is absent, the defined must be absent.
2
Locate the conditions in the passage
Find the sentence where Imam al-Haramayn states that the definition is not complete except by these two conditions.
3
Apply the conditions to a sample definition
Take a typical usuli definition, e.g., 'Riba is an excess without a valid counter-value' and test it: does every case of excess without counter-value count as riba (ittiraad)? Does every absence of such excess mean no riba (in'ikaas)?
4
Identify potential violations
Consider definitions that may be too broad (fail ittiraad) or too narrow (fail in'ikaas).

Why Legal Theorists Reject Composite Definition (Tarkib)
Author surveys methods of discovering definition and explains why usuliyyun reject composite tarkib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Islamic legal theorists (usuliyyun) rejected the Aristotelian method of composite definition, citing specific scholars and their reasoning.

Core Idea
For usuliyyun, a definition must be simple; composite definitions blur the line between definition and description.

This passage surveys the four methods for discovering definition—induction, division, demonstration, and composition—and reveals a major divergence: while Aristotle and the Islamic Peripatetics favoured composition (genus + differentia), the legal theorists and many theologians rejected it. Understanding the reasons behind this rejection illuminates the Islamic epistemological insistence on definitional purity and precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four methods of discovering definition
List the four methods mentioned: istiqra' (induction), qisma (division), burhan (demonstration), and tarkib (composition). Note which method Aristotle adopted and which he refuted.
These methods are found in Islamic commentaries on Aristotelian logic.
2
Contrast Aristotle's position with the usuli position
Aristotle and the Peripatetics considered tarkib (genus + differentia) essential. The usuliyyun, however, rejected it as a valid method for definition.
This is a key epistemological divergence between falsafa and usul al-fiqh.
3
Understand the usuli condition: definition must not be composite
Al-Zarkashi states that one condition of definition for usuliyyun is that it be non-composite. Theologians forbade combining multiple attributes unless necessary.
The shift: what logicians see as necessary, theologians see as problematic.
4
Analyze al-Ash'ari's definition of 'body'
Al-Ash'ari defined body as 'long, broad, deep'—three dimensions combined. He normally forbade composite definitions but allowed this because no single dimension alone distinguishes body from other things.
This shows that even the strictest theologians allowed composition when simplification is impossible.
5
Recognize the broader consensus among theologians
Ibn Taymiyya reports that all classes of theologians—Mu'tazilites, Shiites, Ash'arites—forbade mentioning shared attributes in a definition.
This consensus shows the rejection of tarkib is not a marginal view but a mainstream usuli principle.

وإذا كان الحد عند المسلمين هو التمييز بين المحدود وغيره ـ فما هي طريقة اكتشافه؟ قد رأينا طرقاً كثيرة لاكتشاف الحد عند الشراح الإسلاميين للمنطق الأرسططاليسي، وهذه الطرق هي الاستقراء والقسمة والبرهان والتركيب. وقد رأينا أن هذه الطريقة الأخيرة هي التي لجأ إليها أرسطو مع نقضه للطرق الأخرى. وتابعه المشاؤون الإسلاميون متابعة تامة. ورأينا بعض المفكرين الإسلاميين يأخذون بالطرق الأخرى وعلى خلاف مذهب أرسطو. أما الأصوليون فلم يقبلوا شيئاً من هذه الطرق ـ وخاصة طريق التركيب عند أرسطو. يقول الزركشي إن من شروط الحد عند الأصوليين « أن لا يكون مركباً على خلاف وتفصيل، فعند المنطقيين لا بد في الحد من التركيب ومنعه المتكلمون » ثم يذكر أن إمام الحرمين نقل هذا عن كثير من المتكلمين وينقل الزركشي أيضاً عن الأستاذ أبي منصور « اختلف أصحابنا في تركيب الحد من وصفين فأكثر فمنع أبو الحسن الأشعري الجمع بين معنيين في حد واحد إذا أمكن إفراد أحد المعنيين عن الآخر. ولهذا اختار في حد الجسم أنه الطويل العريض العميق » ويقرر ابن تيمية أن عامة نظار المسلمين « منعوا أن يذكر في الحد الصفات المشتركة بينه وبين غيره » ويقول ابن تيمية أن جميع طبقات المتكلمين صرحوا بهذا ـ معتزلة ( أبو هاشم الجبائي ) وشيعة ( ابن النوبختي ) وأشاعرة ( الباقلاني ) وقد رأينا الأشعري ( ٣٢٤هـ ـ ٩٣٥م ) لا
And if definition among Muslims is the distinction between the defined and other things—then what is the method of discovering it? We have seen many methods for discovering definition among the Islamic commentators of Aristotelian logic: these methods are induction (istiqra'), division (qisma), demonstration (burhan), and composition (tarkib). We have seen that the last method is the one Aristotle resorted to, while refuting the other methods. The Islamic Peripatetics followed him completely. We have seen some Islamic thinkers adopting the other methods contrary to Aristotle's position. As for the legal theorists, they did not accept any of these methods—especially the method of composition from Aristotle. Al-Zarkashi says that among the conditions of definition for the legal theorists is 'that it not be composite, according to disagreement and detail. For the logicians, composition is necessary in the definition, but the theologians forbid it.' Then he mentions that Imam al-Haramayn transmitted this from many theologians. Al-Zarkashi also transmits from al-Ustadh Abu Mansur: 'Our companions differed about composing the definition from two or more descriptions. Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari forbade combining two meanings in one definition if it is possible to isolate one meaning from the other. Hence he chose for the definition of body that it is long, broad, and deep.' Ibn Taymiyya states that the general body of Muslim theoreticians 'forbade mentioning in the definition the attributes shared between it and other things.' Ibn Taymiyya says that all classes of theologians expressed this—Mu'tazilites (Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i), Shiites (Ibn al-Nawbakht), and Ash'arites (al-Baqillani). And we have seen al-Ash'ari (324 AH - 935 CE) not...
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage discusses the methods used to discover a definition and the rejection of composite definition (tarkib) by Islamic legal theorists (usuliyyun). The author begins by noting that if definition is simply distinguishing the defined from other things, then what method is used to discover it? He lists four methods found among Islamic commentators on Aristotelian logic: induction (istiqra'), division (qisma), demonstration (burhan), and composition (tarkib). Aristotle himself adopted composition while refuting the others, and the Islamic Peripatetics followed him. Some Islamic thinkers, however, adopted other methods. The legal theorists rejected all these methods, especially composition. Al-Zarkashi is quoted stating that one condition of definition for the legal theorists is that it not be composite; the logicians require composition, but the theologians forbid it. This is transmitted from Imam al-Haramayn and many theologians. Further, al-Zarkashi quotes Abu Mansur about a disagreement among scholars: al-Ash'ari forbade combining two meanings in a single definition if one meaning could stand alone. For instance, al-Ash'ari defined body as 'long, broad, and deep'—a composite definition (three dimensions) but necessary because each dimension alone does not distinguish body. Ibn Taymiyya then asserts that the majority of Muslim theorists—including Mu'tazilites like Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i, Shiites like Ibn al-Nawbakht, and Ash'arites like al-Baqillani—forbade mentioning attributes common with other things in a definition. The passage ends with a brief mention of al-Ash'ari, though the sentence is incomplete. Overall, the passage illustrates the usuli insistence on a simple, non-composite definition using a single distinguishing property, unlike the Aristotelian composite of genus and differentia.

Key Terms
التركيب
الاستقراء
القسمة
البرهان

B) Because each dimension alone cannot distinguish body from other things
C) Because he followed Aristotle
D) Because he rejected three-dimensional objects

Key Takeaway
Islamic legal theorists and theologians rejected composite definition to maintain definitional purity, but allowed necessary complexity when simplicity was impossible.

?

Redefining Definition: Hadd as Tamyiz in Islamic Logic
Author contrasts Aristotelian definition with Islamic view and asks about method of discovery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Islamic concept of hadd as tamyiz from the Aristotelian definition as essence-revealing, and identify the four methods of discovering definition discussed in the passage.

Core Idea
For Muslims, a definition does not need to reveal essence — it need only distinguish the defined from everything else.

The passage begins by contrasting Aristotelian and Islamic definitions. The Aristotelian hadd aims to reveal the essence (mahiyya), making it extremely difficult. In contrast, Islamic scholars redefined hadd simply as tamyiz — a non-essential distinction between the defined and other things, which is much easier to attain. But if definition is merely distinction, then how do we discover it? The author lists four methods found in Islamic commentaries: induction, division, demonstration, and composition. We will see which of these were accepted by the mutakallimun and usuliyyun.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing conceptions of hadd
In the Arabic, locate where the author contrasts the Aristotelian definition (المعرف للماهية) with the Islamic definition (التمييز غير الذاتي). Note the difference in purpose.
The Aristotelian definition aims at essence; the Islamic at distinction.
2
Extract the four methods of discovering hadd
Find the list: الاستقراء، القسمة، البرهان، التركيب. Understand each term's basic meaning.
These are induction, division, demonstration, and composition.
3
Compare Aristotle's choice with the Islamic Peripatetic position
The passage says Aristotle resorted to composition (تركيب) and the Peripatetics followed him. What does this reveal about their method?
Aristotle and his followers favored composition.
4
Identify the position of Muslim usuliyyun
According to al-Zarkashi, what condition do usuliyyun place on hadd? (It must not be composite.) How does this differ from the logicians?
Usuliyyun reject composition entirely.

فصعوبة التوصل إلى الحد إذن ناتجة من تعريف الحد الأرسططاليسي من أنه المعرف للماهية . أما إذا كان قصد به التمييز غير الذاتي بين المحدود وغيره ، كان في غاية السهولة . وإذا كان الحد عند المسلمين هو التمييز بين المحدود وغيره ـ فما هي طريقة اكتشافه ؟ قد رأينا طرقاً كثيرة لاكتشاف الحد عند الشراح الإسلاميين للمنطق الأرسططاليسي ، وهذه الطرق هي الاستقراء والقسمة والبرهان والتركيب . وقد رأينا أن هذه الطريقة الأخيرة هي التي لجأ اليها أرسطو مع نقضه للطرق الأخرى . وتابعه المشاؤون الإسلاميون متابعة تامة . ورأينا بعض المفكرين الإسلاميين يأخذون بالطرق الأخرى وعلى خلاف مذهب أرسطو . أما الأصوليون فلم يقبلوا شيئاً من هذه الطرق ـ وخاصة طريق التركيب عند أرسطو. يقول الزركشي إن من شروط الحد عند الأصوليين « أن لا يكون مركباً على خلاف وتفصيل، فعند المنطقيين لا بد في الحد من التركيب ومنعه المتكلمون » ثم يذكر أن إمام الحرمين نقل هذا عن كثير من المتكلمين وينقل الزركشي أيضاً عن الأستاذ أبي منصور « اختلف أصحابنا في تركيب الحد من وصفين فأكثر فمنع أبو الحسن الأشعري الجمع بين معنيين في حد واحد إذا أمكن إفراد أحد المعنيين عن الآخر. ولهذا اختار في حد الجسم أنه الطويل العريض العميق ويقرر ابن تيمية أن عامة نظار المسلمين «منعوا أن يذكر في الحد الصفات المشتركة بينه وبين غيره » ويقول ابن تيمية أن جميع طبقات المتكلمين صرحوا بهذا ـ معتزلة ( أبو هاشم الجبائي ) وشيعة ( ابن النوبختي ) وأشاعرة ( الباقلاني ) وقد رأينا الأشعري لا يقبل أيضاً فكرة التركيب .
The difficulty of arriving at the definition (hadd) therefore results from the Aristotelian definition of hadd as that which makes known the essence. But if the intention with it is the non-essential distinction between the defined and other things, then it is extremely easy. And if hadd according to the Muslims is the distinction between the defined and other things, then what is its method of discovery? We have seen many methods for discovering hadd among the Islamic commentators on Aristotelian logic, and these methods are induction, division, demonstration, and composition. And we have seen that this last method is the one to which Aristotle resorted while refuting the other methods. And the Islamic Peripatetics followed him completely. And we have seen some Islamic thinkers adopting the other methods contrary to Aristotle's doctrine. As for the usuliyyun (scholars of usul), they did not accept any of these methods — especially the method of composition according to Aristotle. Al-Zarkashi says that among the conditions of hadd according to the usuliyyun is 'that it not be composite, according to a dispute and detail; for according to the logicians, composition is necessary in hadd, and the mutakallimun have prohibited it.' Then he mentions that Imam al-Haramayn reported this from many mutakallimun. Al-Zarkashi also reports from al-Ustadh Abu Mansur: 'Our companions disagreed about composing the hadd from two or more descriptions. Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari forbade combining two meanings in a single hadd if it is possible to isolate one of the two meanings from the other. For this reason, he chose in defining body that it is long, wide, deep.' And Ibn Taymiyya affirms that the generality of the theoretical scholars (nuzzar) among the Muslims 'prohibited mentioning in the hadd the attributes common between it and other things.' And Ibn Taymiyya says that all classes of mutakallimun have stated this — Mu'tazila (Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i), Shi'a (Ibn al-Nawbakht), and Ash'ariyya (al-Baqillani). And we have seen that al-Ash'ari also does not accept the idea of composition.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition of the Islamic conception of definition (hadd). The author begins by contrasting the Aristotelian notion of definition as that which reveals essence with the Islamic view that definition is merely a distinction (tamyiz) between the defined and other things, which is much easier to achieve. He then raises the question: if definition is distinction, what method discovers it? He lists the four methods found in Islamic commentaries on Aristotle: induction (istiqra'), division (qisma), demonstration (burhan), and composition (tarkib). The author notes that Aristotle himself preferred composition and refuted the others, and the Islamic Peripatetics followed him, though some Islamic thinkers accepted the other methods. Crucially, the usuliyyun (scholars of usul al-fiqh and kalam) rejected all these methods, especially composition. The author supports this with quotations. Al-Zarkashi is cited stating that a condition of definition for usuliyyun is that it not be composite, contrary to logicians who require composition. Then al-Zarkashi reports from Abu Mansur that al-Ash'ari forbade combining two meanings in one definition if separable; for example, he defined body as 'long, wide, deep' — three distinct attributes. Ibn Taymiyya adds that all Muslim theoretical scholars (nuzzar) prohibited mentioning common attributes in definition, across all schools: Mu'tazila, Shi'a, and Ash'ariyya. Thus, al-Ash'ari himself is shown to reject composition, establishing a unified Islamic position against the Aristotelian composite definition.

Key Takeaway
Islamic definition is not about revealing essence but about providing a distinction (tamyiz) that separates the defined from everything else.

Islamic Rejection of Composite Definition (Tarkib)
Author cites scholars' rejection of composite definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the arguments of al-Ash'ari, Ibn Taymiyya, and other mutakallimun against composite definition and explain their reasoning.

Core Idea
The mutakallimun unanimously rejected composing a definition from multiple attributes, especially genus and species.

The passage continues by focusing on the specific rejection of composite definition (tarkib) by Muslim theologians. Al-Zarkashi is quoted stating that for usuliyyun, a condition of hadd is that it not be composite, contrary to the logicians. Al-Ash'ari defined body as 'long, wide, deep' — three separate attributes — because he forbade combining meanings that could be isolated. Ibn Taymiyya confirms that all classes of mutakallimun prohibited mentioning common attributes in a definition, including Mu'tazila, Shi'a, and Ash'ariyya. This lesson examines the grounds for this rejection.

Guided Path
1
Locate al-Zarkashi's condition
In the Arabic, find where al-Zarkashi states 'أن لا يكون مركباً'. What is the condition and who holds it?
Usuliyyun require that definition not be composite.
2
Analyze al-Ash'ari's definition of body
Why did al-Ash'ari define body as 'طويل عريض عميق'? According to the passage, what principle motivated this?
Al-Ash'ari forbade combining two meanings if they can be isolated.
3
Identify the consensus reported by Ibn Taymiyya
Which groups are mentioned as prohibiting common attributes in definition? List them.
Mu'tazila, Shi'a, Ash'ariyya.
4
Understand the logical reason for rejection
Why do mutakallimun reject composition? The passage implies they want to avoid mixing attributes common with other things; definition should be purely distinguishing.
Common attributes do not help in distinction.

Usuliyyun Rejection of Tarkib and Its Causal Basis
Author clarifies what tarkib means and explains its basis in causality and hylomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the usuliyyun's accepted and rejected forms of tarkib (composite definition) and explain the role of causality (al-`illiyya) and hylomorphism in their critique.

Core Idea
The usuliyyun reject only composite definitions that imply a causal relation between genus and differentia.

The author clarifies a key nuance: the usuliyyun do not forbid multiplicity of words in a definition; rather, they reject composition based on essence (matter and form) that implies a causal hierarchy between genus and differentia. This stance is rooted in their rejection of Aristotelian hylomorphism and their own atomistic metaphysics. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the broader conflict between Islamic theology (kalam) and Aristotelian logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of tarkib discussed
The passage distinguishes between composition that is rejected (based on essence/genus+differentia with causal relation) and composition that is accepted (multiplicity of words without causal ordering).
Look for the phrases 'التركيب الذي يبطله الأصوليون' and 'التركيب الذي يقبله الأصوليون'.
2
Understand the basis in causality and hylomorphism
The rejected tarkib rests on the idea that matter (hayula) and form (sura) correspond to genus and species, and that the differentia (fasl) is a cause of the genus (jins). The usuliyyun deny this causal relation.
The text mentions 'فكرة العلية' and 'الهيولي والصورة' as the foundation.
3
Distinguish between logicians' and usuliyyun's composition
Logicians consider jins+fasl as valid in definition. The usuliyyun call the invalid form 'tadakhul al-haqa'iq' (interference of realities), where the essentials are arranged to imply causality, which nullifies the definition.
The quote in the passage: 'مراد المنطقيين بالتركيب هو المركب من جنس وفصل وهو صحيح في الحد...'
4
Recognize the broader intellectual conflict
The rejection of causality in definition led to a severe clash with Aristotelian logic and attacks on philosophers like Ibn Rushd. The Ash'aris are mentioned as not accepting this connection.
The text states: 'أدى إلى تعارض فكري شديد بينهم وبين المنطق الأرسططاليسي...'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن ينبغي أن نلاحظ أنه ليس معنى منع التركيب تكليف الحاد بأن يأتي في حده بعبارة واحدة . « اذ المقصود اتحاد المعنى بدون اللفظ . والعبارات لا تقصد لأنفسها وليست هي حدوداً بل منبئة عن حد » ولكن التركيب الذي يبطله الأصوليون هو المركب من الماهية أي من الجنس والفصل . وهو تركيب يقوم على أساس فكرة العلية ـ فكرة أن للجسم جزئين ـ كالهيولي والصورة غير المحسوستين ـ أي أن الجنس والفصل ـ ينكرهما المتكلمون الذين يقولون « إن الجسم مركب من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ) فالجزء عند المتكلمين لا يكون من مفهوم المسمى أي الجسم لتعقل الجسم دون ذلك الجزء غير المحسوس فالتركيب الذي ينكره الأصوليون ـ هو التركيب المكون من الهيولي والصورة أو الجنس والفصل ـ والتركيب الذي يقبله الأصوليون هو تعدد الألفاظ ولكن لا يجعل الفصل علة للجنس والفصل « مراد المنطقيين بالتركيب هو المركب من جنس وفصل وهو صحيح في الحد والتركيب الذي أراده الأصوليون هو تداخل الحقائق ـ وهو مبطل للحد » . والمقصود بتداخل الحقائق عدم إيراد ذاتيات الحد بوضع الجنس أولاً والفصل ثانياً ـ ثم يكون الفصل علة لوجود الجنس . وقد أدى عدم قبول الأصوليين لفكرة العلل في مبحث الحد وفي غيره من الأبحاث الى تعارض فكري شديد بينهم وبين المنطق الأرسططاليسي كما أدى الى مهاجمة الفلاسفة وعلى الاخص ابن رشد ، لهم هجوماً عنيفاً . وصلة مبحث العلل بالحد ـ عند أرسطو صلة وثيقة ـ فان الحد الارسططاليسي للشيء يتكون من مادته وصورته أي من جنسه وفصله . وذلك أن الحد إنما وضع ليبين حقيقة الشيء ـ والصورة هي كمال وجود الشيء وهي أشرف ما به قوامه . وينقد الأصوليون مبحث الحد من حيث اتصاله بمبحث العلل . إن الأشاعرة لم
But it should be noted that the prohibition of composition does not require the definer to bring in his definition a single expression. 'For the purpose is the unity of meaning without the wording. Expressions are not intended for themselves, and they are not definitions but indicators of definitions.' But the composition that the usuliyyun invalidate is that which is composed of the essence, i.e., genus and species. It is a composition based on the idea of causality — the idea that the body has two parts, like matter and form which are not perceived — i.e., genus and species — the mutakallimun deny them, saying: 'The body is composed of indivisible parts.' So the part according to the mutakallimun is not from the concept of the named thing, i.e., the body, because the body is understood without that imperceptible part. So the composition which the usuliyyun deny is the composition consisting of matter and form, or genus and species. And the composition which the usuliyyun accept is multiplicity of words, but they do not make the differentia a cause of the genus. 'The logicians' intended meaning by composition is the composite of genus and species, and it is valid in definition. But the composition intended by the usuliyyun is the interference of realities (tadakhul al-haqa'iq), and it nullifies the definition.' And the meaning of interference of realities is that the essentials of definition are not presented by placing the genus first and the differentia second — then the differentia would be a cause for the existence of the genus. The usuliyyun's rejection of the idea of causes in the topic of definition and in other discussions led to a severe intellectual conflict between them and Aristotelian logic, and it also led to violent attacks on the philosophers, especially Ibn Rushd. The connection of the topic of causes with definition, according to Aristotle, is a close one. For the Aristotelian definition of a thing consists of its matter and form, i.e., its genus and species. And that is because definition is only put to clarify the reality of a thing, and form is the perfection of a thing's existence and is the noblest constituent. And the usuliyyun critique the topic of definition concerning its connection to the topic of causes. The Ash'aris did not...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage clarifies and deepens the earlier discussion of tarkib. The author begins by noting that forbidding composition in definition does not mean the definer must use a single word; the point is unity of meaning, not wording. He quotes a source stating that expressions are merely indicators of definitions, not definitions themselves. The specific composition invalidated by the usuliyyun is that based on essence, i.e., genus (jins) and differentia (fasl). This composition rests on the idea of causality: the belief that a body has two imperceptible parts — matter (hayula) and form (sura) — which correspond to genus and species. The mutakallimun deny this, holding that a body is composed of indivisible atoms (juz' la yatajazza'), and that the concept of body is understood without those parts. Thus, the composition rejected is the one involving matter and form (or genus and species). In contrast, the usuliyyun accept multiplicity of words in a definition as long as the differentia is not made a cause of the genus. The author then quotes a distinction: logicians' composition (jins+fasl) is valid, but what usuliyyun call 'tadakhul al-haqa'iq' (interference of realities) — presenting essentials in a way that implies causality — nullifies definition. The cause of the conflict is the rejection of causality (al-`illa) in definition and elsewhere, which led to intense intellectual opposition to Aristotelian logic and harsh attacks on philosophers, particularly Ibn Rushd. The author explains that for Aristotle, definition is intimately tied to causality, as it consists of matter and form (genus and species), and form is the perfection of essence. The Ash'aris, the passage concludes, did not [accept this? — the text cuts off]. Thus, the passage highlights the fundamental clash between Islamic theology (kalam) and Aristotelian metaphysics in the realm of definition.

Key Terms
التركيب
تداخل الحقائق
العلية
الهيولي والصورة
الجنس والفصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of the usuliyyun's rejection of composite definition (tarkib)?
A) They require definitions to be single words.
B) They reject the idea of genus and species altogether.
C) They reject the causal relation (i.e., making the differentia a cause of the genus) and the underlying hylomorphic theory.
D) They only accept definitions from revealed texts.

Key Takeaway
The usuliyyun reject tarkib only when it implies a causal relation between genus and differentia, rooted in Aristotelian hylomorphism; they accept multiplicity of words without causal ordering.

The Two Types of Composition in Definition
Author distinguishes acceptable verbal multiplicity from rejected causal composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the composition accepted by usuliyyun (verbal multiplicity) and the composition they reject (causal genus-differentia) in definition.

Core Idea
Usuliyyun reject causal composition but accept verbal multiplicity in definition.

This passage clarifies a key point of conflict between Islamic legal theorists and Aristotelian logicians. The usuliyyun do not reject all composition; they allow multiple words as long as the differentia is not a cause of the genus. Understanding this distinction is crucial for analyzing definitions in usul al-fiqh, where definitions must avoid metaphysical commitments about parts of essence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' view of composition
Read the passage: the logicians' composition is genus and differentia based on causality (matter and form). Find the phrase 'التركيب الذي يبطله الأصوليون هو المركب من الماهية أي من الجنس والفصل' which describes the rejected composition.
2
Identify the usuliyyun's acceptance of verbal multiplicity
The passage says they accept 'multiplicity of words' (تعدد الألفاظ) but reject that the differentia causes the genus. Look for 'يقبل... تعدد الألفاظ ولكن لا يجعل الفصل علة للجنس'.
3
Understand the basis of rejection
The usuliyyun deny that the body has imperceptible parts (matter and form); they hold to atomism. So they cannot accept a definition based on such metaphysics. This is stated in: 'الجزء عند المتكلمين لا يكون من مفهوم المسمى'.
4
Connect to causality
The usuliyyun's rejection of causality in definition aligns with their rejection of causality in general (Ash'arite occasionalism). The passage mentions: 'عدم قبول الأصوليين لفكرة العلل في مبحث الحد وفي غيره'.

يقبل أيضاً فكرة التركيب ، ولكن ينبغي أن نلاحظ أنه ليس معنى منع التركيب تكليف الحاد بأن يأتي في حده بعبارة واحدة . « اذ المقصود اتحاد المعنى بدون اللفظ . والعبارات لا تقصد لأنفسها وليست هي حدوداً بل منبئة عن حدود »(۱) ولكن التركيب الذي يبطله الأصوليون هو المركب من الماهية أي من الجنس والفصل . وهو تركيب يقوم على أساس فكرة العلية ـ فكرة أن للجسم جزئين ـ كالهيولي والصورة غير المحسوستين ـ أي أن الجنس والفصل ـ ينكرهما المتكلمون الذين يقولون « إن الجسم مركب من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ) فالجزء عند المتكلمين لا يكون من مفهوم المسمى أي الجسم لتعقل الجسم دون ذلك الجزء غير المحسوس (۲) فالتركيب الذي ينكره الأصوليون ـ هو التركيب المكون من الهيولي والصورة أو الجنس والفصل ـ والتركيب الذي يقبله الأصوليون هو تعدد الألفاظ ولكن لا يجعل الفصل علة للجنس والفصل « مراد المنطقيين بالتركيب هو المركب من جنس وفصل وهو صحيح في الحد والتركيب الذي أراده الأصوليون هو تداخل الحقائق ـ وهو مبطل للحد (۳) . والمقصود بتداخل الحقائق عدم إيراد ذاتيات الحد بوضع الجنس أولاً والفصل ثانياً ـ ثم يكون الفصل علة لوجود الجنس . وقد أدى عدم قبول الأصوليين لفكرة العلل في مبحث الحد وفي غيره من الأبحاث الى تعارض فكري شديد بينهم وبين المنطق الأرسططاليسي كما أدى الى مهاجمة الفلاسفة وعلى الاخص ابن رشد ، لهم هجوماً عنيفاً . وصلة مبحث العلل بالحد ـ عند أرسطو صلة وثيقة ـ فان الحد الارسططاليسي للشيء يتكون من مادته وصورته أي من جنسه وفصله . وذلك أن الحد إنما وضع ليبين حقيقة الشيء ـ والصورة هي كمال وجود الشيء وهي أشرف ما به قوامه . وينقد الأصوليون مبحث الحد من حيث اتصاله بمبحث العلل . إن الأشاعرة لم يوفقوا على فكرة العلية في أبحاثهم العقلية هذا ، من ناحية ـ ومن ناحية أخرى يستند على مذهب العلل عنصرا الحد أي الجنس والفصل . ولم يقبل الأصوليون فكرة الجنس والفصل ، فكان من المعقول ألا يقبلوا الاساس الذي تستند عليه فكرتهما .وقد أثار بعض الأصوليين المتأخرين الذين لم يقبلوا ـ فيما يرجح ـ المنطق الأرسططاليسي اعتراضات هامة على استناد الحد الارسططاليسي على فكرة العلل(١) . تتلخص في أن الارسططاليسيين يرون أن الفصل وهو الصورة علة وجود الجنس وهو المادة(٢) لامتناع وجود جنس مجرد من الفصول كالحيوانية المطلقة ، ولكن الرازي لا يوافق على هذا « لأن الماهية المركبة من ذات وصفة أخص منها كالحيوان الكاتب يكون الذات جنسها والصفة فصلها مع امتناع كون الصفة علة للذات لتأخرها »(٣) وينبغي أن نلاحظ أن الرازي يعتبر الكاتب « فصلاً » بينما هي « خاصة » أي أنه يتكلم من ناحية أن الماهية اعتبارية ، بينما المناطقة الارسططاليسيون يتطلبون الماهية حقيقية ، وقد نشأ عن أخذ المناطقة بالعلية في الحد واعتبار الفصل علة للجنس وإبطال الأصوليين لها النتائج الآتية :أولاً ـ يرى الأصوليون « أن الفصل الواحد بالنسبة إلى نوع واحد قد يكون جنساً له » فالناطق بالنسبة إلى أنواع الحيوان فصل للإنسان وإلى الملك جنس له . والحيوان جنس للإنسان . لأن هذه الكلمة تطلق على أفراد حقيقة مختلفة ، ولكنها في الوقت عينه تفصل الإنسان من الملك . أما الأرسططاليسيون فيرون أن الفصل الواحد بالنسبة إلى النوع الواحد لا يكون جنساً باعتبار آخر ، لأن الفصل لو كان جنساً لكان معلولاً للجنس المعلول له ـ
It also accepts the idea of composition, but it must be noted that the meaning of prohibiting composition is not to oblige the definer to come up with his definition in a single phrase. 'For the intended is the unity of meaning without the word. Expressions are not intended for themselves and are not definitions but indicate definitions' (1). But the composition that the usuliyyun invalidate is that composed of the quiddity, i.e., of genus and differentia. It is a composition based on the idea of causality — the idea that the body has two parts — like the imperceptible matter and form — i.e., genus and differentia — which the mutakallimun deny because they say 'the body is composed of indivisible parts.' For the part according to the mutakallimun is not from the concept of the named, i.e., the body, because the body can be conceived without that imperceptible part (2). So the composition that the usuliyyun deny is the composition consisting of matter and form or genus and differentia. And the composition that the usuliyyun accept is multiplicity of words but they do not make the differentia a cause of the genus, and the differentia: 'The logicians' intended meaning by composition is that composed of genus and differentia, and this is correct in definition, while the composition intended by the usuliyyun is the interpenetration of realities — and this invalidates the definition' (3). And the intended meaning of interpenetration of realities is not bringing the essentials of the definition by placing the genus first and the differentia second — then the differentia becomes a cause for the existence of the genus. The usuliyyun's non-acceptance of the idea of causes in the topic of definition and in other investigations led to a severe intellectual conflict between them and Aristotelian logic, and also led to a violent attack by the philosophers, especially Ibn Rushd, against them. The connection between the topic of causes and definition according to Aristotle is a close connection — for the Aristotelian definition of a thing consists of its matter and its form, i.e., its genus and its differentia. That is because definition is only established to explain the reality of a thing — and form is the perfection of the thing's existence and it is the noblest thing by which it is constituted. The usuliyyun criticize the topic of definition in its connection with the topic of causes. The Ash'arites did not agree on the idea of causality in their intellectual investigations — this, on one hand — and on the other hand, the two elements of definition, i.e., genus and differentia, are based on the doctrine of causes. And the usuliyyun did not accept the idea of genus and differentia, so it was reasonable that they would not accept the basis upon which their idea rests. Some later usuliyyun who, it is likely, did not accept Aristotelian logic raised important objections to the dependence of the Aristotelian definition on the idea of causes (1). They summarize that the Aristotelians see that the differentia, which is form, is the cause of the existence of the genus, which is matter (2), because it is impossible for a genus devoid of differentiae to exist, like absolute animality. But al-Razi disagrees with this 'because the quiddity composed of a self and a more specific attribute, like the writing animal, has the self as its genus and the attribute as its differentia, while it is impossible for the attribute to be a cause of the self because it is posterior' (3). It must be noted that al-Razi considers 'writing' a 'differentia' while it is a 'property' — that is, he speaks from the perspective that the quiddity is a mental consideration, while the Aristotelian logicians require a real quiddity. The following results arose from the logicians' adoption of causality in definition and considering the differentia as a cause of the genus, and from the usuliyyun's invalidation of it: First — the usuliyyun see 'that the same differentia relative to a single species may be a genus for it.' So 'rational' relative to the species animal is a differentia for man, and relative to angel is a genus for it. And 'animal' is a genus for man. Because this term is applied to individuals of different realities, but at the same time it distinguishes man from angel. As for the Aristotelians, they see that the same differentia relative to one species cannot be a genus under another consideration, because if the differentia were a genus it would be an effect of the genus that is an effect of it —
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage critically examines the conflict between Islamic legal theorists (usuliyyun) and Aristotelian logicians over the nature of definition (hadd), specifically concerning composition (tarkib) and causality ('illa). The author begins by clarifying that the usuliyyun's rejection of composition does not mean a definition must be a single word; rather, they object to definitions composed of genus (jins) and differentia (fasl) as understood through matter and form (hayula and sura), which are imperceptible. The usuliyyun deny that a body has such parts and instead hold to atomism. They accept only verbal multiplicity without treating the differentia as a cause of the genus. The author explains that the logicians' composition is valid in definition, but the usuliyyun reject 'interpenetration of realities' (tadakhul al-haqa'iq), where the differentia is made a cause of the genus. This rejection stems from the usuliyyun's broader denial of causal relationships in intellectual matters, which leads to a clash with Aristotle's view that definition consists of matter and form (genus and differentia). The Ash'arites, in particular, rejected causality, and thus rejected the basis of genus and differentia. Later usuliyyun raised objections: Aristotelians hold that the differentia (form) is a cause of the genus (matter) because a bare genus cannot exist. Al-Razi objects, using the example of 'writing animal' (al-hayawan al-katib) — here 'animal' is the genus and 'writing' the differentia, but writing cannot be a cause of animal since it is a later attribute. The author notes that al-Razi treats 'writing' as a differentia when it is actually a property (khassa), indicating he speaks of mental quiddity while Aristotelians require real quiddity. The first consequence of this disagreement is that usuliyyun hold that one differentia can be a genus for a species under another aspect — e.g., 'rational' is a differentia for man but a genus for angel. Aristotelians deny this because it would entail that the differentia is both cause and effect of the same genus, which is impossible in a causal framework.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of composition do usuliyyun accept in definitions?
A) Composition based on matter and form
B) Verbal multiplicity without causal hierarchy
C) Single-word definitions only
D) Genus and differentia as causes

Key Takeaway
The usuliyyun accept definitions with multiple words but reject the causal composition where the differentia is a cause of the genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the definition 'salah is a collection of dhikr, qiyam, ruku', sujud, etc.,' determine whether this definition involves a causal composition (rejected by usuliyyun) or merely verbal multiplicity. Explain.
?
Construct a definition of 'zakat' (obligatory charity) that follows the usuliyyun's acceptable composition: use multiple words but ensure that no part is considered a cause of another.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
10 min
Al-Razi's Objection and the Flexibility of Differentia
Al-Razi objects to causal definition and shows differentia can be a genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate al-Razi's objection that the differentia cannot be a cause of the genus and explain how one differentia can serve as a genus for another species.

Core Idea
Al-Razi shows that the 'differentia' is often a property and cannot be a cause; it can also be a genus under a different perspective.

This passage presents a nuanced critique by al-Razi against the Aristotelian causal definition. Using the example 'writing animal', he argues that the attribute (writing) cannot be a cause of the self (animal). Moreover, he shows that the same term can function as a differentia for one species and a genus for another, challenging the fixed hierarchy of genus and differentia. This lesson examines these arguments and their implications for defining concepts in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Examine al-Razi's example: 'al-hayawan al-katib'
The passage introduces the example 'الحيوان الكاتب' (the writing animal). Identify the two parts: 'حيوان' (animal) as the self (dhat) and 'كاتب' (writing) as the attribute (sifa).
2
Understand al-Razi's argument
Al-Razi argues that the attribute (writing) is posterior to the self (animal), so it cannot be a cause of the self. The text says: 'امتناع كون الصفة علة للذات لتأخرها'.
3
Note the shift in perspective: mental vs real quiddity
The passage notes that al-Razi treats 'writing' as a differentia while Aristotelians would call it a property (khassa). This shows a difference in considering quiddity as mental (i'tibari) vs real (haqiqi). The text says: 'الرازي يعتبر الكاتب فصلاً بينما هي خاصة'.
4
Apply the usuliyyun's view of flexible differentia
The usuliyyun hold that one differentia can be a genus under another aspect. Example: 'ناطق' (rational) is a differentia for man but a genus for angel. The passage states: 'الفصل الواحد بالنسبة إلى نوع واحد قد يكون جنساً له'.

Al-Razi objects, using the example of 'writing animal' (al-hayawan al-katib) — here 'animal' is the genus and 'writing' the differentia, but writing cannot be a cause of animal since it is a later attribute. The author notes that al-Razi treats 'writing' as a differentia when it is actually a property (khassa), indicating he speaks of mental quiddity while Aristotelians require real quiddity. The first consequence of this disagreement is that usuliyyun hold that one differentia can be a genus for a species under another aspect — e.g., 'rational' is a differentia for man but a genus for angel. Aristotelians deny this because it would entail that the differentia is both cause and effect of the same genus, which is impossible in a causal framework.

الجنس

الماهية الحقيقية

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's objection shows that the differentia cannot be a cause of the genus, and one differentia can serve as a genus for another species, challenging the Aristotelian hierarchy.

The Usuliyyun Critique of Aristotelian Definition
Author sets up the conflict over causality in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Usuliyyun's objection to the Aristotelian definition based on causality and reconstruct al-Razi's counterargument.

Core Idea
The Usuliyyun reject the Aristotelian definition because it wrongly treats the differentia as the cause of the genus.

The Usuliyyun (Islamic legal theorists) did not simply ignore Aristotelian logic; they critically engaged with its metaphysical foundations. In this passage, the author explains why they rejected the Aristotelian theory of definition (hadd) which is built on the doctrine of causality. At the heart of the dispute is whether the differentia (fasl) can be considered the cause of the genus (jins). We will examine the objection raised by some later Usuliyyun and the specific counterargument from Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing camps
The Aristotelians hold that definition is based on causality: the differentia (form) causes the genus (matter). The Usuliyyun reject this framework. Notice the phrase 'مذهب العلل عنصرا الحد' indicating the basis of definition on causes.
2
Understand the Aristotelian position
Aristotelians argue that the differentia is the cause of the existence of the genus because a genus cannot exist without a differentia (e.g., 'animal' must be specified as 'rational' or 'non-rational'). This is a metaphysical claim about real essences.
The text says: 'الفصل وهو الصورة علة وجود الجنس وهو المادة'.
3
Examine al-Razi's objection
Al-Razi argues that in a composite essence like 'rational animal', the genus (animal) is the essence and the differentia (rational) is an attribute. The attribute is posterior to the essence, so it cannot be its cause. This is a logical rather than temporal posteriority.
Al-Razi's phrase: 'لأن الماهية المركبة من ذات وصفة أخص منها ... مع امتناع كون الصفة علة للذات لتأخرها'.
4
Note the conceptual vs. real essence distinction
The author points out that al-Razi treats 'rational' as a differentia, but in Aristotelian logic it is a property (khassa). This difference arises because al-Razi considers the essence as conceptual (i'tibari), whereas Aristotelians require it to be real (haqiqi). This subtlety explains the disagreement.
The text: 'الرازي يعتبر الكاتب فصلا بينما هي خاصة' and 'يتكلم من ناحية أن الماهية اعتبارية'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوافقوا على فكرة العلية في أبحاثهم العقلية هذا ، من ناحية ـ ومن ناحية أخرى يستند على مذهب العلل عنصرا الحد أي الجنس والفصل . ولم يقبل الأصوليون فكرة الجنس والفصل ، فكان من المعقول ألا يقبلوا الاساس الذي تستند عليه فكرتهما . وقد أثار بعض الأصوليين المتأخرين الذين لم يقبلوا ـ فيما يرجح ـ المنطق الأرسططاليسي اعتراضات هامة على استناد الحد الارسططاليسي على فكرة العلل(١) . تتلخص في أن الارسططاليسيين يرون أن الفصل وهو الصورة علة وجود الجنس وهو المادة(٢) لامتناع وجود جنس مجرد من الفصول كالحيوانية المطلقة ، ولكن الرازي لا يوافق على هذا « لأن الماهية المركبة من ذات وصفة أخص منها كالحيوان الكاتب يكون الذات جنسها والصفة فصلها مع امتناع كون الصفة علة للذات لتأخرها »(٣) وينبغي أن نلاحظ أن الرازي يعتبر الكاتب « فصلاً » بينما هي « خاصة » أي أنه يتكلم من ناحية أن الماهية اعتبارية ، بينما المناطقة الارسططاليسيون يتطلبون الماهية حقيقية ، وقد نشأ عن أخذ المناطقة بالعلية في الحد واعتبار الفصل علة للجنس وإبطال الأصوليين لها النتائج الآتية :
They agree on the idea of causality in their intellectual investigations, on one hand, and on the other hand it is based on the doctrine of causes as the two elements of definition, namely genus and differentia. The Usuliyyun did not accept the idea of genus and differentia, so it was reasonable for them not to accept the basis on which their concept is founded. Some later Usuliyyun who presumably did not accept Aristotelian logic raised important objections against the reliance of the Aristotelian definition on the idea of causes. It can be summarized as that the Aristotelians hold that the differentia, which is the form, is the cause of the existence of the genus, which is the matter, because it is impossible for a genus devoid of differentiae to exist, like absolute animality. But al-Razi does not agree with this, 'because the essence composed of an essence and a more specific attribute, like the rational animal, has the essence as its genus and the attribute as its differentia, while it is impossible for the attribute to be a cause of the essence because it is posterior to it.' It should be noted that al-Razi considers 'rational' as a differentia while it is a property (special characteristic), i.e., he speaks from the perspective that the essence is conceptual, while the Aristotelian logicians require the essence to be real. And from the adoption of causality by logicians in definition and considering the differentia as a cause of the genus, and the Usuliyyun's refutation of it, the following results emerged:
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage introduces the conflict between the Usuliyyun (Islamic legal theorists) and the Aristotelians over the foundation of definition (hadd). The author states that the Usuliyyun reject the Aristotelian framework that bases definition on the metaphysical doctrine of causes, where the genus (jins) is like matter and the differentia (fasl) is like form, and the differentia is considered the cause of the genus. The passage mentions that some later Usuliyyun, who presumably did not accept Aristotelian logic, raised important objections. Specifically, the Aristotelians argue that the differentia is the cause of the existence of the genus, as it is impossible for a genus to exist without a differentia (e.g., absolute animality cannot exist without a specific differentia like rationality). However, Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi disagrees, arguing that in a composite essence like the rational animal, the essence (animal) is the genus and the attribute (rational) is the differentia, but the attribute cannot be a cause of the essence because it is posterior to it. The author notes that al-Razi treats 'rational' as a differentia, while actually it is a special property (khassa), and this is because al-Razi considers the essence as conceptual (i'tibari), whereas the Aristotelians require the essence to be real (haqiqi). Consequently, the logicians' adoption of causality in definition and the Usuliyyun's refutation led to the following four results, which will be elaborated in subsequent lessons.

The First Usuli Objection: Differentia as Genus
Author presents the first Usuli objection: a single differentia can be a genus for another species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the Usuli objection against the Aristotelian causal link between genus and differentia and identify the logical problem of circular causality.

Core Idea
The Usuliyyun free the differentia from being an 'effect' of the genus.

This lesson presents the first objection raised by the Usuliyyun (Islamic legal theorists) against the Aristotelian definitional framework. The Aristotelians hold that a differentia cannot serve as a genus for another species because it would create a circular causal relationship. The Usuliyyun disagree, using the example of 'rational' to show that a term can function as both a differentia and a genus in different contexts. Understanding this objection is crucial for appreciating how Islamic scholars adapted Greek logic to fit their own epistemological commitments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views
Locate the positions of the Usuliyyun and the Aristotelians in the passage. The Usuliyyun claim that a single differentia can be a genus relative to another species. The Aristotelians deny this.
2
Analyze the Usuli example
The passage gives 'natiq' (rational) as an example: it is a differentia for human (distinguishing humans from other animals) and a genus for angel (since angels are rational). How does this undermine the Aristotelian view?
The key is that the same term has two different 'relational' roles.
3
Understand the Aristotelian objection
The Aristotelians argue that if a differentia were a genus, it would be an effect (ma'lul) of the genus it differentiates, leading to the effect being a cause of its own cause, which is impossible. Trace this causal chain in the passage.
They see genus and differentia as matter and form, with the genus being potential and the differentia actualizing it.
4
Evaluate the logical consequence
Reflect on why the Usuliyyun do not accept this objection. They do not adopt the metaphysical framework where genus and differentia are causally linked as potentiality and actuality. Therefore, for them, no logical contradiction arises.
This shows how different philosophical assumptions lead to different logical conclusions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولاً ـ يرى الأصوليون « أن الفصل الواحد بالنسبة إلى نوع واحد قد يكون جنساً له » فالناطق بالنسبة إلى أنواع الحيوان فصل للإنسان وإلى الملك جنس له . والحيوان جنس للإنسان . لأن هذه الكلمة تطلق على أفراد حقيقة مختلفة ، ولكنها في الوقت عينه تفصل الإنسان من الملك . أما الأرسططاليسيون فيرون أن الفصل الواحد بالنسبة إلى النوع الواحد لا يكون جنساً باعتبار آخر ، لأن الفصل لو كان جنساً لكان معلولاً للجنس المعلول له ـ فكون المعلول علة لعلته ـ وهو ممتنع(١) .
First – The Usuliyyun hold that 'a single differentia relative to one type can be a genus for it.' For example, 'rational' (al-natiq) relative to the types of animal is a differentia for human and a genus for angel. And animal is a genus for human. Because this word applies to individuals of different realities, but at the same time it distinguishes human from angel. As for the Aristotelians, they hold that a single differentia relative to one type cannot be a genus from another consideration, because if the differentia were a genus, it would be an effect of the genus which is its cause – thus the effect would be a cause of its cause – and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection of the Usuliyyun against the Aristotelian definition based on causality. The Usuliyyun argue that a single differentia (fasl) can serve as a genus (jins) for another species. They give the example of 'rational' (natiq): relative to the types of animal, 'rational' is a differentia for the species 'human' (since it distinguishes humans from other animals), but at the same time, 'rational' can be considered a genus for the species 'angel' (since angels are rational beings). Similarly, 'animal' is a genus for human. The word 'rational' applies to individuals of different realities (humans and angels), yet it also differentiates human from angel. The Aristotelians, however, maintain that the same differentia cannot also be a genus, because if it were a genus, it would be an effect of the genus it differentiates, leading to a circular causality where the effect becomes the cause of its own cause – which is impossible. This highlights the core disagreement: the Usuliyyun do not accept the metaphysical causal framework that links genus and differentia as matter and form, so they see no problem with a single term functioning as both differentia and genus in different contexts.

Key Takeaway
The Usuliyyun challenge the Aristotelian causal link between genus and differentia, arguing that a term can function as both depending on the species it is related to.
